                             Administration
   APPROVED FOR                                                       ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                             Brian King, Chancellor                   INFORMATION


BACKGROUND:
Pursuant to the provisions of AB 2910, Chapter 1486, Statutes of 1986, each quarter districts must report
their financial condition on forms prescribed by the California Community Colleges Chancellor’s Office.
This prescribed report (form CCFS-311Q) must be submitted to the Chancellor’s Office and to the County
Superintendent of Schools within forty-five (45) days following the end of each quarter for the first three
quarters. The fourth quarter is reported on the CCFS-311 Annual Financial and Budget Report, which
must be submitted by October 10th each year. The Chancellor’s Office staff will then review the
prescribed quarterly reports and notify districts if further action is necessary.


STATUS:
In accordance with AB 2910, the Governing Board should review the enclosed prescribed report (CCFS-
311Q) at a regularly scheduled meeting and enter the report as part of the minutes of the meeting. As
required, the District’s Chief Executive Officer (Chancellor) and Chief Business Officer have certified that
the information for the quarter ended September 30, 2025, contained in this report is correct.


RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees receive the September 30, 2025, Quarterly Financial Status
Report (CCFS-311Q) and the related financial statements.

                               Administration
   APPROVED FOR                                                            ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                               Brian King, Chancellor                      INFORMATION

BACKGROUND:
In 1998, the District and Los Rios Colleges Foundation (Foundation) adopted a Master Agreement whereby the
Foundation became an auxiliary organization of the district. All college foundations’ investment activities were
combined under the Foundation. Morgan Stanley is the investment consultant for the Foundation.

As an auxiliary organization, the Foundation is not required to operate under GC 53600 investment restrictions.
The Foundation Board has a Statement of Rules, Objectives and Guidelines (Statement) to govern the investment
of funds, last revised June 2018. The funds should be invested with care, skill, prudence, and diligence with the
goal of producing returns equal to or exceeding prevailing standards among foundations of similar asset size, as
well as for the protection of funds held in perpetual duration. The Statement defines the investment guidelines
for specified asset classes for endowed funds as follows: equities, defined as common stock, convertible preferred
stock, convertible bonds, and convertible stock, shall represent 25-60% of the total fund assets; fixed-income
securities, defined as investments with maturities greater than one year that pay a fixed rate of return, shall
represent 17-50% of the total assets; alternative investments, defined as fund-of-fund investments, shall
represent up to 20% of the total fund assets; and cash, defined as maturities shorter than one year, shall represent
2-10% of the total fund assets. In addition, the Statement provides guidelines for investing non-endowed funds
based upon the purpose of the donation and the horizon of time for the use of funds. The three non-endowed
portfolio funds available are cash management, fixed income, and balanced funds.

STATUS:
The Foundation Quarterly Investment Report, including realized and unrealized earnings, represents the
investment activity for the quarter ended June 30th. The Los Rios Colleges Foundation Finance Committee directs
the investments of the Foundation. The return for the quarter ended for the endowed portfolio of $22.4 million
was 4.55% compared to 5.04% for the composite benchmark. The return for the quarter ended for the total
managed portfolio of $30.0 million was 3.59% compared to 3.93% for the composite benchmark. In accordance
with generally accepted accounting principles, investments are restated to market value as of each fiscal year-
end.


RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees receive the Foundation Quarterly Investment Report for the quarter
ended September 30, 2025.

   SUBJECT:                  Disposition of Surplus Equipment –        ATTACHMENT: None
                             Salvage Value Greater than $5,000
                                                                       ENCLOSURE:       None
                                                                       STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 5
   AGENDA ITEM:              Consent Item J                            TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:

                                                                       CONSENT/ROUTINE                 X
   RECOMMENDED BY:           Mario Rodriguez, Executive Vice
                             Chancellor, Finance and                   FIRST READING
                             Administration
   APPROVED FOR                                                        ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                             Brian King, Chancellor                    INFORMATION


BACKGROUND:
The Education Code regulates the procedure by which a community college district can dispose of real
and personal property. Education Code section 81450-81450.5 provides that the governing board may,
sell for cash, exchange for value or donate any personal property belonging to the district if the property
is not required for school purposes, or if it should be disposed of for the purpose of replacement, or if it
is unsatisfactory or not suitable for school use. The methods for disposal differ based upon the estimated
value of the equipment. Whereas, most equipment is disposed of either through the State of California
or, if the State will not accept, through a scrap dealer, items with a value greater than $5,000 either
individually or in aggregate, require a public auction, noticed as required by law.

STATUS:
The District will auction the following items which in aggregate have a value greater than $5,000:
Kioto KL249 (8381); Taylor Dunn B2-48 TT (9519); Ford E150 Passenger Van (9250); 2005 Ford Crown
Victoria (9502); 2008 Ford Crown Victoria (9346). Due to the poor condition of the items, the equipment
is no longer suitable for school use. The District, via public auction, intends to sell to the highest bidder
or donate to an interested school/public entity.

RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees approve the disposal of the listed item per Education Code
section 81450-81450.5.

                                                                                                          HOME

                LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                                 DATE: November 12, 2025

   SUBJECT:                  Disposition of Surplus Equipment        ATTACHMENT: None

   APPROVED FOR                                                      ACTION

                             Brian King, Chancellor                  INFORMATION

BACKGROUND:
The Education Code regulates the procedures by which a Community College District can dispose of real
and personal property. Education Code section 81452 provides that the governing board may, by
unanimous vote, dispose of items valued at $5,000 or less by private sale without advertising or selling
the items at public auction. The District has held previous auctions, but they generally cost more than
they have netted for the District.

STATUS:
The District has a quantity of surplus materials that needs to be disposed of, such as outdated desks and
computers. The District has located a scrap dealer who will take selected surplus items for recycling.
Any items remaining will be disposed.

The surplus items to be recycled or disposed of are either irreparable, obsolete, in poor condition or not
needed for district/college operations and include the following: 114 computers; 1 copier; 70 laptops; 1
manikin; 1 medication dispensing system; 1 modem; 31 monitors; 4 printers; 1 projector and 2 vitals
machines.

These items have a value of less than $5,000.


RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees approve the disposal of the listed items per Education
Code section 81452.

                                                                                                 207
                                                                                                           HOME

                LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                                 DATE: November 12, 2025

   SUBJECT:                  2025-2026 Sabbaticals/Professional       ATTACHMENT: Yes
                             Development Leaves
                                                                      ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                      STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 3
   AGENDA ITEM:              Consent Item N                           TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:


                             Mario Rodriguez, Executive Vice          CONSENT/ROUTINE                 X
   RECOMMENDED BY:           Chancellor of Finance and
                             Administration                           FIRST READING

   APPROVED FOR                                                       ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                             Brian King, Chancellor                   INFORMATION


BACKGROUND:
The agreement with the Los Rios College Federation of Teachers (LRCFT) provides the calculation
used to determine the number of professional development leaves be granted each year. Type A
leaves are leaves of one semester at full pay or one year at half pay. Type B leaves are reassigned
time for up to 100% and for up to one year in duration.

The agreement with the LRCFT permits the Professional Standards Committee at each college to
recommend the conversion of one or more Type A sabbaticals into equivalent FTE of Type B leaves.

Sabbatical/professional development leave recommendations are presented to the Board in April
and November of each year.
The purpose and scope for leaves, as stated in the LRCFT agreement (11.6.4) are as follows:
   1. Retraining of applicant to allow for new assignment(s) in a needed area as
       determined by College and District priorities.
   2. Studies, projects or activities that provide staff with opportunities to upgrade academic,
       technical, and vocational skills and knowledge for current or future assignments.
   3. Studies, projects, or activities for the improvement and/or innovation of curriculum,
       educational delivery systems, student personnel services, or other support services.
   4. Studies, projects, or activities for development or revision of certificate or degree
       programs.
   5. Studies, projects, or activities related to feasibility or revision of new or existing programs.
   6. Studies, projects, or activities for the enhancement of student access and success at the
       course, department program or institutional, or community college system levels.
   7. Studies, projects, or activities that support completion of college and/or District goals,
      objectives and priorities.
RECOMMENDATION:

It is recommended that the attached sabbatical/professional development leaves be approved by the
Board of Trustees for the 2025-2026 year.

Type A Leave Time                                                                        Annual FTE

Joshua Weiner              History Professor            100%          Spring 2026          .500 FTE
“Source book of Modern World History: Alternate Pasts/Better Futures”
Proposal: Equitable and anti-racist education is a crucial component of ARC's mission. Low or
zero cost textbooks can be a means of addressing equity, but that alone is insufficient unless
the content is inclusive and adopts and explicit framework of anti-racism. Based on my earlier
work on an OER world history textbook dedicated to equity, anti-racism, and social justice, I
propose to create an OER Primary Source reader for the Modern World History survey
(HIST308). I am proposing a primary source reader instead of a textbook for several reasons:
first, because of its versatility. Instructors can use it as their main text, as a supplement to other
materials, or even as a resource for themselves that they don't assign in their course.
Primary sources also have the benefit of bringing the voices of historical actors directly to
students rather than those voices being mediated by textbook authors. Additionally, a reader
allows me to carefully select the sources to emphasize people and perspectives that have
typically been ignored or underrepresented in more traditional materials. A final benefit comes
from the fact that the reader will be housed in a digital environment. That will allow any
instructors who adopt it the ability to provide students with a range of sources in multiple
mediums: written documents, art and architecture, photographs, artifacts, and even films and
recorded speeches.


                   Zero (0) Type A Leave(s) unused during 2025/26
   .0 FTE Type A Leave to be carried forward to 2026/27 (per LRCFT Section 11.6.8.5)



Type B Leave Time                                                                        Annual FTE

Heidi Bennett            Business Professor              80%          Spring 2026          .400 FTE
“LinkedIn at American River College”
Proposal: The purpose of this proposal is to ensure the full integration, community
engagement, and campus-wide awareness of LinkedIn Learning and LinkedIn Talent Insights
at American River College. These tools, funded through a trial period extending to 2028, provide
 transformative resources for students, faculty, and staff. By establishing a strong foundation of
adoption and measurable outcomes at ARC, this project will demonstrate sustainability and
support recommendations for potential expansion across the Los Rios Community College
District or statewide to all California community colleges.




                                                                                                 209
                                                                                                  HOME
                                  Fall 2025 Board Agenda
                                     Sabbatical Leaves

Sharleen McCarroll           Math Professor           26.7%        Spring 2026       .133 FTE
“Accessible, Zero-Cost MLC Canvas Courses for Math 333 and MathS 333”
Proposal: The Math Learning Center (MLC) supports roughly 500 students each fall and spring
and about 150 in summer—approximately 1,000 unique students annually. Currently, students
must purchase a $120 access code to use MLC course materials, resulting in about $60,000
each fall and spring semester (≈$120,000 per year) in out-of-pocket costs. To eliminate these
costs and deliver materials that better meet students’ needs, the MLC is transitioning to high-
quality Open Educational Resources (OER) that are fully integrated with Canvas and compliant
with ADA/Section 508 accessibility standards. While OER are free to students, they require
significant faculty time to develop and remediate, especially in STEM, where most existing OER
were not created with accessibility in mind.

Type A Leave Time                                                                  Annual FTE

Roy Simpson           Mathematics             100%          Spring 2026      .500 FTE
                      Professor
“The CRC Math Ecosystem: An AI-Powered OER Initiative for Student Success and Equity”
Proposal: This project completes and integrates a comprehensive, AI-powered learning
ecosystem for CRC's entire mathematics pathway for STEM students (Math 372, 373, 375,
384, 400, 401), leveraging the six OER textbooks and online homework systems. The
sabbatical focuses on three innovative components: (1) building a 'Corequisite Codex' for on-
demand, just-in-time remediation; (2) deploying a custom 'Hawk AI Tutor' in every course
section for 24/7 student support; and (3) creating a novel AI-assessment system to provide
data-driven instructional insights for faculty. This project moves beyond zero-cost textbooks to
provide a total, equitable support system that directly addresses the academic preparedness
gaps resulting from AB 705 and 1705. By providing immediate, targeted support, this project
directly addresses the academic preparedness gaps many students face and eliminates all
textbook and online homework costs for the entire math pathway for STEM students, removing
a significant financial barrier. By creating a fully integrated, 100% curriculum-aligned OER and
AI ecosystem, this project establishes CRC and the Los Rios District as a national leader in
mathematics education and technological innovation. It provides a sustainable, scalable model
for supporting students in the post-AB 1705 era.


                     One (1) Type A Leave unused during 2025/26
 .500 FTE of Type A Leave to be carried forward to 2026/27 (per LRCFT Section 11.6.8.5)

Type B Leave Time                                                                  Annual FTE

Lance Parks              CIS Professor               20%         Spring 2026         .100 FTE
“Redesignating CRC’s Information Systems Security Program as a Center for Academic
Excellence in Cyber Defense”
Proposal: " Lance Parks' and Markus Geissler's joint proposal will help the CISS program to
continue to be at the forefront of cybersecurity education and a leader among California
community colleges (we are only one of eleven colleges with this designation). To maintain
CAE-CD status, the college must be recertified every five years, a labor-intensive process that
takes approximately 300 hours. Profs. Parks and Geissler will be gathering and analyzing data,
writing reports, collaborating with district IT leadership, certifying facility readiness, and
participating in faculty interviews as part of the process. The CAE-CD designation, which our
CISS program has held since 2021, has benefited our college by enhancing our reputation and
providing opportunities for collaboration with other CAE institutions. Our students have
benefited from greater eligibility for scholarships, employment opportunities, and a competitive
edge in the job market for a critical, in-demand profession.

Noah Gardner              Biology Assistant         20%          Spring 2026        .100 FTE
                          Professor
“Strengthening CRC botany’s connection to students’ lives by incorporating hands-on
gardening experience”
Proposal: This project entails Prof. Gardner completing the UC Master Gardener certification
program. This will entail weekly coursework from January to April 2026. After completing the
Master Gardener course, he will draw from his experiences to improve the CRC California
Native Garden and other campus facilities and develop hands-on gardening course projects
and outreach opportunities for botany students. This will include time spent inventorying
specimens in our Native Garden and identifying any need for replacement, meeting and working
with horticulture department to develop materials, meeting with connections at UC to consult
and solicit donations, developing curriculum and course materials including lesson plans,
assessments, and at least one pilot run for new activities. Giving students the opportunity to
apply botany to their lived experience makes our campus and community a better place and
allows them to see themselves in the curriculum. This will also serve our students outside the
classroom, through campus projects such as Native Garden maintenance and campus facilities
improvement which improve student life.

Daniel Considine          Philosophy Professor         50%         Spring 2026         .250 FTE
                                                       50%          Fall 2026          .250 FTE
“Notes on Kant’s Prolegomena”
Proposal: This project is for the benefit both of my students who are assigned this text in their
philosophy courses, and myself as an instructor and scholar who teach this text. Kant’s
language is notoriously difficult and inaccessible, yet his ideas are profoundly important; I hope
to bridge these two issues by providing a reference guide to students when they are struggling
to understand a primary text. This project would enhance student access and success at the
departmental and program levels. Moreover, this project improves my academic and vocational
skills for my current assignment.

Andreas Bazos             Mathematics and              20%        Spring 2026      .100 FTE
                          Statistics Professor
“Complete Overhaul of Stats C1000 and Stat 10 Canva Course for EOPS, VAKA, UMOJA
and PUENTE programs”
Proposal: We created our Stat C1000 and Stat 10 program for the online world during COVID
in Fall of 2020 and we now need to redo it to make it more up-to-date, with changes to the
outline for common course numbering, current events/data, as well as social justice issue
surrounding the groups we are teaching it too, and current technologies. These classes were
fully online and now are finally going back to fully in person and we need to employ different
techniques for that. We will be redoing most of our 100 or more videos embedded in Canvas
along with redoing the more than 100 assignments and assessments. This class will be a flipped
model class, and we will also be creating the in-class group work assignments and activities to
help engage our students, utilizing strategies and techniques we have learned in recent
professional developments and research.

experiences. Yet, such opportunities consistently lead to increased engagement, persistence,

                LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                               DATE: November 12, 2025

   SUBJECT:                 Formation of the K-16 Collaborative     ATTACHMENT: None
                            Joint Powers Authority (JPA)
                                                                    ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                    STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 1,2,4
   AGENDA ITEM:             Action Item A                           TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:

                                                                    CONSENT/ROUTINE
   RECOMMENDED BY:          Gabe Ross, Chief Strategy and
                                                                    FIRST READING
                            Communications Officer
   APPROVED FOR                                                     ACTION                          X
   CONSIDERATION:
                            Brian King, Chancellor                  INFORMATION


BACKGROUND:
In 2022, Los Rios was the lead agency in forming the Sacramento K-16 Collaborative, a partnership
between higher education, K-12 County Offices of Education, individual districts and schools,
employers, and community organizations in the Sacramento Region to address inequalities in
education and employment with an $18.1 million award from the California Regional K-16
Collaboratives Grant Program. Using the grant funding, our district as well as regional partners and
stakeholders aligned across the educational ecosystem to streamline equitable pathways from high
school to postsecondary education and into the workforce.

Since the launch of the K-16 Collaborative grant, the region has made significant progress in closing
equity gaps and strengthening educational and career pathways. Data-sharing agreements now
connect K-12 districts, community colleges, and universities, creating a regional infrastructure that
supports alignment, reduces duplication, and enables longitudinal tracking of student participation,
persistence, transfer, and employment outcomes (including data sharing agreements between Los Rios
and nearly every large district in Sacramento County). Alongside this major achievement, the
Collaborative has driven measurable impact across several other areas. Dual enrollment participation
in our district has nearly doubled from approximately 3,995 to 7,871 learners, expanding access to
early college credit, particularly in underserved districts. New and expanded pathways in healthcare,
engineering and semiconductors, and computing have also been built out at scale, ensuring course
sequences from high school through university are aligned with regional workforce needs and industry
certifications. Enrollment of students of color at our 4-year transfer partners has increased
significantly, with an additional 1,429 young men of color enrolled at Sacramento State and UC Davis.
The Collaborative has also strengthened support for adult learners, launching a highly successful
Comebacker Campaign to re-engage students who had paused their education and emphasize that
returning to college is accessible and achievable. These efforts have tripled the original goal of 2,000
comebackers securing certificates or degrees. Together, these accomplishments demonstrate the
Collaborative’s effectiveness in uniting partners, leveraging data, and accelerating system-wide change
to better serve students and the region’s economy.

                                                                                                   240
                                                                                                          HOME

The Grant Program funding effectively ends June 30, 2026 (with a one-year, no-additional funding
extension to complete grant requirements using remaining, unspent funds by June 30, 2027).

Although the Grant Program funding will end, long-term, sustainable progress requires a stable fiscal
and legal framework for collaboration and ongoing investment. To meet this need, Los Rios and our
partner agencies are proposing to form a joint powers authority (“JPA”) that will, among others:

   •   Continue inter-agency, regional collaboration on career and college pathways initiatives and
       data-sharing and cybersecurity efforts;
   •   Establish a structured repository for any raised funds from other public and private funders;
       and
   •   Provide a budgetary safety net for ongoing, stable operations with contributions from
       participating institutions.

DESCRIPTION OF AGREEMENT:
The Joint Exercise of Powers Act (California Government Code § 6500 et seq.) authorizes public
agencies to agree to jointly exercise their common powers and to create a separate entity to execute
such agreement. The proposed JPA Agreement creates a new public agency called the PK-16
Collaborative Joint Powers Authority or “Collaborative JPA” by January 1, 2026. The JPA structure
enables the infrastructure created by the Collaborative under the State Grant to transition smoothly.
The Collaborative JPA will enable member agencies to develop and sustain college and career
pathways across California’s Capital Region with a focus on student success, while also formally
engaging employers, non-profits, philanthropic donors, and other regional partners to invest
regionally. Such collaborative work would include continuing the data-sharing among educational
institutions and cybersecurity insurance for the collaborative, after the Grant Program ends, in order to
expand dual enrollment opportunities, support high priority student populations, expand transfer
pathways (including reverse transfers), and expand college and career education pathways.

The JPA Agreement creates the Collaborative JPA and sets forth the objectives of the Collaborative JPA
as well as the rights and responsibilities of member agencies. As described in the JPA Agreement, the
Collaborative JPA will be governed by a Board of Directors with each member agency having one
Director and one vote. Los Rios’s Director will be the Chancellor (or designee). Regional partners such
as nonprofits and employers will be non-voting advisory members. The Board of Directors will contract
with an Administrative Firm to provide day-to-day administrative and operational services.

The Administrative Firm will prepare an annual budget to be approved by the Board of Directors in
accordance with its By-Laws. The amount of each party’s annual financial contribution will be
determined by the Board of Directors and will be proportional to each party’s student population. No
later than February 1st of each year, Los Rios shall receive notice of its annual obligation, which may
fluctuate depending on the receipt of sufficient external funding to cover the Collaborative JPA’s
operating budget.

The JPA Board of Directors will hold at least two (2) meetings per year. All meetings of the Board of
Directors will be conducted in accordance with the provisions of the Brown Act (California Government
Code Section 54950 et seq.).

Los Rios’s cost to participate in the JPA is expected not to exceed approximately $2,000 per month and
may be reduced or eliminated entirely upon the receipt of external funding. The JPA Agreement

                                                                                                241
                                                                                                      HOME

provides a process for member agencies to withdraw from the Collaborative JPA. The withdrawing
member agency must provide notice of withdrawal and satisfy any outstanding obligations to the
Collaborative JPA.

RECOMMENDATION:
It is recommended that the Board of Trustees approve and authorize the Los Rios Community College
District entering into the PK-16 Collaborative Joint Powers Authority (JPA); and delegate the Chancellor
to coordinate with other institutions participating in the JPA, negotiate any necessary revisions to
finalize the Agreement, and execute the Agreement if there are at least two other public educational
institutions joining the JPA.




                                                                                               242
                                                                                                               HOME

                 LOS RIOS COMMUNITY COLLEGE DISTRICT
PRESENTED TO BOARD OF TRUSTEES                                                      DATE: November 12, 2025

   SUBJECT:                    Legislative Update                         ATTACHMENT: None
                                                                          ENCLOSURE: None
                                                                          STRATEGIC PLAN GOAL(S): 5
   AGENDA ITEM:                Information Item A                         TYPE OF BOARD CONSIDERATION:


                               Mario Rodriguez, Executive                 CONSENT/ROUTINE
   RECOMMENDED BY:             Vice Chancellor, Finance and
                               Administration                             FIRST READING

   APPROVED FOR                                                           ACTION
   CONSIDERATION:
                               Brian King, Chancellor                     INFORMATION                     X

BACKGROUND:
Annually, staff provides the members of the Board of Trustees with an update on the District’s
government affairs efforts. The District engages MGI Advocacy, led by Mark McDonald, as its outside
state lobbying firm. Mark McDonald’s work for the District is supported by Pamela Lopez of K Street
Consulting, who partners with MGI Advocacy to strengthen strategic communications and legislative
outreach in alignment with District priorities.

STATUS:
MGI Advocacy will provide an update for the Board of Trustees on the District’s government affairs
activities and the key bills of the past legislative year, as well as expectations for the Legislature and
Governor in the coming year. The presentation will include discussion of recently chaptered legislation,
upcoming legislative priorities for 2026, and the results of recent elections with related shifts in
leadership positions as we enter the second year of the 2025–26 legislative session.

RECOMMENDATION:
This item is presented for the Board of Trustees’ information and discussion.

BACKGROUND:
District staff have reviewed the feasibility and operational considerations of live streaming Los Rios
Board of Trustees meetings. The presentation provides context on current meeting practices, associated
technology needs, and potential implementation approaches.

STATUS:
Staff have gathered information on cost estimates, equipment requirements, and logistical implications
related to video streaming options. The Board is being provided this information to inform its discussion.

RECOMMENDATION:
This item is presented for the Board of Trustees’ information and discussion.
